"content-domain": {"domain": [], "crossmark-restriction": false}, "short-container-title": ["Comparative and Functional Genomics"], "published-print": {"date-parts": [[2008]]}, "abstract": "<jats:p>Cohesin is a protein complex that regulates sister chromatid cohesin during cell division. Malfunction in chromatid cohesin results in chromosome missegregation and aneuploidy. Here, we report that mutations of MCD1 and PDS5, two major components of cohesin in budding yeast, cause apoptotic cell death, which is characterized by externalization of phosphatidylserine at cytoplasmic membrane, chromatin condensation and fragmentation, and ROS production. Microarray analysis suggests that the cell death caused by mutation of MCD1 or PDS5 is due to the internal stress response, contrasting to the environmental or external stress response induced by external stimuli, such as hydrogen peroxide. A common feature shared by the internal stress response and external stress response is the response to stimulus, including response to DNA damage, mitochondria functions, and oxidative stress, which play an important role in yeast apoptotic cell death.</jats:p>", "DOI": "10.1155/2008/634283", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2008, 6, 11]], "date-time": Microbiol."], "published-print": {"date-parts": [[2011, 2, 1]]}, "abstract": "<jats:title>ABSTRACT</jats:title><jats:p>In<jats:italic>Corynebacterium glutamicum</jats:italic>, the ArgR protein, a transcriptional repressor, affects the expression level of the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>gene through binding to its promoter region. The<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter region (positions \u221277 to \u221225) has been found by<jats:italic>in vitro</jats:italic>electrophoretic mobility shift assay (EMSA) results and<jats:italic>in silico</jats:italic>analysis to be important for the DNA binding of ArgR. Proline supplementation prevented the DNA binding of ArgR to the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter region and triggered an increase of the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>mRNA level. Additional mutational analyses of the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter region found nucleotides critical for ArgR binding (G located at position \u221258, C at position \u221255, and A at position \u221241 of the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter) in that region. Another transcriptional repressor, FarR, was also demonstrated to bind to the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter region. This binding was delimited to positions \u221257 to \u221277 on the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter. FarR has only one putative binding domain located at positions \u221257 to \u221277, but this region exactly overlapped with the binding region located from positions \u221255 to \u221277 for the binding of ArgR within the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter; thus, if ArgR bound with the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter first, the binding of FarR was not observed in this region. However, if FarR bound to the binding domain located at positions \u221257 to \u221277 first, ArgR could bind other binding sites located at positions \u221249 to \u221225 within the<jats:italic>argB</jats:italic>promoter.
